<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">island state of Australia</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Tasmania_(disambiguation)" title="Tasmania (disambiguation)">Tasmania (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Tasmanian people" redirects here. For "first nation" Tasmanians, see <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Tasmanians" title="Aboriginal Tasmanians">Aboriginal Tasmanians</a>.</div>

<p><b>Tasmania</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> abbreviated as <b>TAS</b> and known colloquially as <b>Tassie</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. It is located 240 km (150 mi) to the south of the <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Australia" title="Mainland Australia">Australian mainland</a>, separated by <a href="/wiki/Bass_Strait" title="Bass Strait">Bass Strait</a>. The state encompasses the main island of Tasmania, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area#Islands_20,000–100,000_km2_(7,700–38,600_sq_mi)" title="List of islands by area">26th-largest island in the world</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Tasmania" title="List of islands of Tasmania">surrounding 334 islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The state has a population of around 526,700<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABSPop_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-ABSPop-1">[1]</a></sup> as of  March 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. Just over forty percent of the population resides in the Greater Hobart precinct, which forms the metropolitan area of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_capital_cities" title="List of Australian capital cities">state capital</a> and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABSCapitalPop_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABSCapitalPop-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tasmania's area is 68,401 km<sup>2</sup> (26,410 sq mi), of which the main island covers 64,519 km<sup>2</sup> (24,911 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> It is promoted as a natural state, and <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Tasmania" title="Protected areas of Tasmania">protected areas of Tasmania</a> cover about 42% of its land area, which includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_parks" title="National parks">national parks</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Wilderness" title="Tasmanian Wilderness">World Heritage Sites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Tasmania was the founding place of the first environmental political party in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>The island is believed to have been occupied by <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> for 30,000 years before British colonisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It is thought <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Tasmanians" title="Aboriginal Tasmanians">Aboriginal Tasmanians</a> were separated from the mainland Aboriginal groups about 10,000 years ago when the sea rose to form Bass Strait.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ryan1_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-ryan1-18">[18]</a></sup> The Aboriginal population is estimated to have been between 3,000 and 7,000 at the time of colonisation, but was almost wiped out within 30 years by a combination of violent guerrilla conflict with settlers known as the "<a href="/wiki/Black_War" title="Black War">Black War</a>", intertribal conflict, and from the late 1820s, the spread of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">infectious diseases</a> to which they had no immunity. The conflict, which peaked between 1825 and 1831, and led to more than three years of martial law, cost the lives of almost 1,100 Aboriginals and settlers.
</p><p>The island was permanently settled by Europeans in 1803 as a <a href="/wiki/Penal_colony" title="Penal colony">penal settlement</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> to prevent claims to the land by the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. The island was initially part of the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_New_South_Wales" title="Colony of New South Wales">Colony of New South Wales</a> but became a separate, self-governing colony under the name <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land" title="Van Diemen's Land">Van Diemen's Land</a> (named after <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Diemen" title="Anthony van Diemen">Anthony van Diemen</a>) in 1825.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Approximately 75,000 <a href="/wiki/Convicts_in_Australia" title="Convicts in Australia">convicts</a> were sent to Van Diemen's Land before transportation ceased in 1853.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1854 the present Constitution of Tasmania was passed, and the following year the colony received permission to change its name to Tasmania. In 1901 it became a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">state</a> through the process of the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">Federation of Australia</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy"><span id="Etymology"></span>Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The state is named after <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Explorer" title="Explorer">explorer</a> <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a>, who made the first reported European sighting of the island on 24 November 1642. Tasman named the island <b>Anthony van Diemen's Land</b> after his sponsor <a href="/wiki/Anthony_van_Diemen" title="Anthony van Diemen">Anthony van Diemen</a>, the Governor of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>. The name was later shortened to <b>Van Diemen's Land</b> by the British. It was officially renamed <b>Tasmania</b> in honour of its first European discoverer on 1 January 1856.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tasmania was sometimes referred to as "Dervon," as mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Jerilderie_Letter" title="Jerilderie Letter">Jerilderie Letter</a> written by the notorious Australian <a href="/wiki/Bushranger" title="Bushranger">bushranger</a> <a href="/wiki/Ned_Kelly" title="Ned Kelly">Ned Kelly</a> in 1879. The colloquial expression for the state is "Tassie". Tasmania is also colloquially shortened to "Tas," mainly when used in business names and website addresses. TAS is also the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_postal_abbreviations" title="Australian postal abbreviations">Australia Post abbreviation</a> for the state.
</p><p>The reconstructed <a href="/wiki/Palawa_kani" title="Palawa kani">Palawa kani</a> language name for Tasmania is <i><b>Lutriwita</b></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tasmania" title="History of Tasmania">History of Tasmania</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_history">Physical history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Physical history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Tasmania" title="Geology of Tasmania">Geology of Tasmania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tessellated_Pavement_Sunrise_Landscape.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2391" data-file-width="3587" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Tessellated_Pavement_Sunrise_Landscape.jpg/220px-Tessellated_Pavement_Sunrise_Landscape.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Tessellated_Pavement_Sunrise_Landscape.jpg/330px-Tessellated_Pavement_Sunrise_Landscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Tessellated_Pavement_Sunrise_Landscape.jpg/440px-Tessellated_Pavement_Sunrise_Landscape.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tessellated_Pavement_Sunrise_Landscape.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tessellated_pavement" title="Tessellated pavement">Tessellated pavement</a>, a rare rock formation on the <a href="/wiki/Tasman_Peninsula" title="Tasman Peninsula">Tasman Peninsula</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Autumn-in-Tasmania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Autumn-in-Tasmania.jpg/220px-Autumn-in-Tasmania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Autumn-in-Tasmania.jpg/330px-Autumn-in-Tasmania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Autumn-in-Tasmania.jpg/440px-Autumn-in-Tasmania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Autumn-in-Tasmania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">Autumn</a> on the <a href="/wiki/River_Derwent_(Tasmania)" title="River Derwent (Tasmania)">Derwent River</a> in Tasmania</div></div></div>
<p>The island was adjoined to the mainland of <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> until the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a> about 10,000 years ago. Much of the island is composed of <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> <a href="/wiki/Diabase" title="Diabase">dolerite</a> intrusions (the upwelling of <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">magma</a>) through other rock types, sometimes forming large columnar joints. Tasmania has the world's largest areas of dolerite, with many distinctive mountains and cliffs formed from this rock type. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Plateau_(Tasmania)" title="Central Plateau (Tasmania)">central plateau</a> and the southeast portions of the island are mostly dolerites. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Wellington_(Tasmania)" title="Mount Wellington (Tasmania)">Mount Wellington</a> above <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a> is a good example, showing distinct columns known as the Organ Pipes.
</p><p>In the southern midlands as far south as Hobart, the dolerite is underlaid by <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> and similar sedimentary stones. In the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Precambrian" title="Precambrian">Precambrian</a> <a href="/wiki/Quartzite" title="Quartzite">quartzites</a> were formed from very ancient sea sediments and form strikingly sharp ridges and ranges, such as Federation Peak or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frenchmans_Cap,_Tasmania" title="Frenchmans Cap, Tasmania">Frenchmans Cap</a>.
</p><p>In the northeast and east, continental <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granites</a> can be seen, such as at Freycinet, similar to coastal granites on mainland Australia. In the northwest and west, mineral-rich volcanic rock can be seen at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Read_(Tasmania)" title="Mount Read (Tasmania)">Mount Read</a> near <a href="/wiki/Rosebery,_Tasmania" title="Rosebery, Tasmania">Rosebery</a>, or at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Lyell,_Tasmania" title="Mount Lyell, Tasmania">Mount Lyell</a> near <a href="/wiki/Queenstown,_Tasmania" title="Queenstown, Tasmania">Queenstown</a>. Also present in the south and northwest is <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> with caves.
</p><p>The quartzite and dolerite areas in the higher mountains show evidence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glaciation" title="Glaciation">glaciation</a>, and much of Australia's glaciated landscape is found on the Central Plateau and the Southwest. <a href="/wiki/Cradle_Mountain" title="Cradle Mountain">Cradle Mountain</a>, another dolerite peak, for example, was a <a href="/wiki/Nunatak" title="Nunatak">nunatak</a>. The combination of these different rock types contributes to scenery which is distinct from any other region of the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the far southwest corner of the state, the geology is almost wholly quartzite, which gives the mountains the false impression of having snow-capped peaks year round.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_people">Indigenous people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Indigenous people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Aborigines" title="Tasmanian Aborigines">Tasmanian Aborigines</a></div>
<p>Evidence indicates the presence of <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians" title="Aboriginal Australians">Aborigines</a> in Tasmania about 42,000 years ago. Rising sea levels cut Tasmania off from mainland Australia about 10,000 years ago and by the time of European contact, the Aboriginal people in Tasmania had nine major nations or ethnic groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ryan1_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-ryan1-18">[18]</a></sup> At the time of the British occupation and colonisation in 1803, the indigenous population was estimated at between 3,000 and 10,000. Historian Lyndall Ryan's analysis of population studies led her to conclude that there were about 7,000 spread throughout the island's nine nations;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lyndall_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-lyndall-23">[23]</a></sup> Nicholas Clements, citing research by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Plomley" title="Brian Plomley">N.J.B. Plomley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhys_Jones_(archaeologist)" title="Rhys Jones (archaeologist)">Rhys Jones</a>, settled on a figure of 3,000 to 4,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> They engaged in <a href="/wiki/Fire-stick_farming" title="Fire-stick farming">fire-stick farming</a>, hunted game including kangaroo and wallabies, caught seals, mutton-birds, shellfish and fish and lived as nine separate "nations" on the island, which they knew as "Trouwunna".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival_and_governance">European arrival and governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: European arrival and governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2310" data-file-width="2916" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png/220px-Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png/330px-Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png/440px-Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thevenot_-_Hollandia_Nova_detecta_1644.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Melchisedech Thevenot (1620?–1692): Map of New Holland 1644, based on a map by the Dutch cartographer Joan Blaeu.</div></div></div>
<p>The first reported sighting of Tasmania by a <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a> was on 24 November 1642 by Dutch explorer <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a>, who landed at today's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackman_Bay" title="Blackman Bay">Blackman Bay</a>. More than a century later, in 1772, a French expedition led by <a href="/wiki/Marc-Joseph_Marion_du_Fresne" title="Marc-Joseph Marion du Fresne">Marc-Joseph Marion du Fresne</a> landed at (nearby but different) <a href="/wiki/Blackmans_Bay,_Tasmania" title="Blackmans Bay, Tasmania">Blackmans Bay</a>, and the following year <a href="/wiki/Tobias_Furneaux" title="Tobias Furneaux">Tobias Furneaux</a> became the first Englishman to land in Tasmania when he arrived at <a href="/wiki/Adventure_Bay,_Tasmania" title="Adventure Bay, Tasmania">Adventure Bay</a>. Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Adventure_Bay,_Tasmania" title="Adventure Bay, Tasmania">Adventure Bay</a> in 1777. Matthew Flinders and <a href="/wiki/George_Bass" title="George Bass">George Bass</a> sailed through <a href="/wiki/Bass_Strait" title="Bass Strait">Bass Strait</a> in 1798–99, determining for the first time that Tasmania was an island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes121_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-hughes121-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Glover_-_Mount_Wellington_and_Hobart_Town_from_Kangaroo_Point_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2563" data-file-width="5191" decoding="async" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/John_Glover_-_Mount_Wellington_and_Hobart_Town_from_Kangaroo_Point_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-John_Glover_-_Mount_Wellington_and_Hobart_Town_from_Kangaroo_Point_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/John_Glover_-_Mount_Wellington_and_Hobart_Town_from_Kangaroo_Point_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-John_Glover_-_Mount_Wellington_and_Hobart_Town_from_Kangaroo_Point_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/John_Glover_-_Mount_Wellington_and_Hobart_Town_from_Kangaroo_Point_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-John_Glover_-_Mount_Wellington_and_Hobart_Town_from_Kangaroo_Point_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Glover_-_Mount_Wellington_and_Hobart_Town_from_Kangaroo_Point_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Wellington_(Tasmania)" title="Mount Wellington (Tasmania)">Mount Wellington</a> and Hobart from Kangaroo Point, c. 1834</div></div></div>
<p>Sealers and whalers based themselves on Tasmania's islands from 1798,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and in August 1803 <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> Governor <a href="/wiki/Philip_Gidley_King" title="Philip Gidley King">Philip King</a> sent Lieutenant <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Bowen_(colonist)" title="John Bowen (colonist)">John Bowen</a> to establish a small military outpost on the eastern shore of the <a href="/wiki/River_Derwent_(Tasmania)" title="River Derwent (Tasmania)">Derwent River</a> in order to forestall any claims to the island by French explorers who had been exploring the southern Australian coastline. Bowen, who led a party of 49, including 21 male and three female convicts, named the camp Risdon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes121_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-hughes121-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Several months later a second settlement was established by Captain <a href="/wiki/David_Collins_(lieutenant_governor)" title="David Collins (lieutenant governor)">David Collins</a>, with 308 convicts, 5 kilometres (3.1 mi) to the south in <a href="/wiki/Sullivans_Cove" title="Sullivans Cove">Sullivans Cove</a> on the western side of the Derwent, where fresh water was more plentiful. The latter settlement became known as Hobart Town or Hobarton, later shortened to <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Colonies" title="Secretary of State for the Colonies">British Colonial Secretary</a> of the time, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Hobart" title="Lord Hobart">Lord Hobart</a>. The settlement at Risdon was later abandoned. Left on their own without further supplies, the Sullivans Cove settlement suffered severe food shortages and by 1806 its inhabitants were starving, with many resorting to scraping seaweed off rocks and scavenging washed-up whale blubber from the shore to survive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes121_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-hughes121-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>A smaller colony was established at Port Dalrymple on the Tamar River in the island's north in October 1804 and several other convict-based settlements were established, including the particularly harsh <a href="/wiki/Penal_colony" title="Penal colony">penal colonies</a> at <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur,_Tasmania" title="Port Arthur, Tasmania">Port Arthur</a> in the southeast and <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Harbour" title="Macquarie Harbour">Macquarie Harbour</a> on the West Coast. Tasmania was eventually sent 75,000 convicts—four out of every ten people transported to <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes121_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-hughes121-25">[25]</a></sup> By 1819 the Aboriginal and British population reached parity with about 5000 of each, although among the colonists men outnumbered women four to one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parity_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-parity-28">[28]</a></sup> Wealthy middle-class free settlers began arriving in large numbers from 1820, lured by the promise of land grants and free convict labour. Settlement in the island's northwest corner was monopolised by the <a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land_Company" title="Van Diemen's Land Company">Van Diemen's Land Company</a>, which sent its first surveyors to the district in 1826. By 1830 one-third of Australia's non-Indigenous population lived in Van Diemen's Land and the island accounted for about half of all land under cultivation and exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Black_War">Black War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Black War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Black_War" title="Black War">Black War</a></div>
<p>Tensions between Tasmania's black and white inhabitants rose, partly driven by increasing competition for kangaroo and other game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Explorer and naval officer <a href="/wiki/John_Oxley" title="John Oxley">John Oxley</a> in 1810 noted the "many atrocious cruelties" inflicted on <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Aboriginals</a> by convict <a href="/wiki/Bushranger" title="Bushranger">bushrangers</a> in the north, which in turn led to black attacks on solitary white hunters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Hostilities increased further with the arrival of 600 colonists from <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a> between 1807 and 1813. They established farms along the River Derwent and east and west of <a href="/wiki/Launceston,_Tasmania" title="Launceston, Tasmania">Launceston</a>, occupying 10 percent of Van Diemen's Land. By 1824 the colonial population had swelled to 12,600, while the island's sheep population had reached 200,000. The rapid colonisation transformed traditional kangaroo hunting grounds into farms with grazing livestock as well as fences, hedges and stone walls, while police and military patrols were increased to control the convict farm labourers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Violence began to spiral rapidly from the mid-1820s in what became known as the "<a href="/wiki/Black_War" title="Black War">Black War</a>". While black inhabitants were driven to desperation by dwindling food supplies as well as anger at the prevalence of abductions of women and girls, whites carried out attacks as a means of exacting revenge and suppressing the native threat. Van Diemen's Land had an enormous gender imbalance, with male colonists outnumbering females six to one in 1822—and 16 to one among the convict population. Historian Nicholas Clements has suggested the "voracious appetite" for native women was the most important trigger for the explosion of violence from the late 1820s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Truganini_and_last_4_tasmanian_aborigines.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="892" data-file-width="916" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Truganini_and_last_4_tasmanian_aborigines.jpg/170px-Truganini_and_last_4_tasmanian_aborigines.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Truganini_and_last_4_tasmanian_aborigines.jpg/255px-Truganini_and_last_4_tasmanian_aborigines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Truganini_and_last_4_tasmanian_aborigines.jpg/340px-Truganini_and_last_4_tasmanian_aborigines.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Truganini_and_last_4_tasmanian_aborigines.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Four elderly full-blood <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Aborigines" title="Tasmanian Aborigines">Tasmanian Aborigines</a> c. 1860s. <a href="/wiki/Truganini" title="Truganini">Truganini</a>, for many years claimed to be the last full-blood Aboriginal to survive, is seated at far right.</div></div></div>
<p>From 1825 to 1828 the number of native attacks more than doubled each year, raising panic among settlers. Over the summer of 1826–7 clans from the Big River, Oyster Bay and North Midlands nations speared stock-keepers on farms and made it clear that they wanted the settlers and their sheep and cattle to move from their kangaroo hunting grounds. Settlers responded vigorously, resulting in many mass-killings. In November 1826 Governor <a href="/wiki/Sir_George_Arthur,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir George Arthur, 1st Baronet">George Arthur</a> issued a government notice declaring that colonists were free to kill Aborigines when they attacked settlers or their property and in the following eight months more than 200 Aborigines were killed in the Settled Districts in reprisal for the deaths of 15 colonists. After another eight months the death toll had risen to 43 colonists and probably 350 Aboriginals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Almost 300 British troops were sent into the Settled Districts, and in November 1828 Arthur declared martial law, giving soldiers the right to shoot on sight any Aboriginal in the Settled Districts. Martial law would remain in force for more than three years, the longest period of martial law in Australian history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 1830 Arthur organised the so-called "Black Line", ordering every able-bodied male colonist to assemble at one of seven designated places in the Settled Districts to join a massive drive to sweep Aboriginals out of the region and on to the <a href="/wiki/Tasman_Peninsula" title="Tasman Peninsula">Tasman Peninsula</a>. The campaign failed and was abandoned seven weeks later, but by then Tasmania's Aboriginal population had fallen to about 300.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Removal_of_Aborigines">Removal of Aborigines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Removal of Aborigines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>After hostilities between settlers and Aboriginals ceased in 1832, almost all of the remnants of the indigenous population were persuaded or forced by government agent <a href="/wiki/George_Augustus_Robinson" title="George Augustus Robinson">George Augustus Robinson</a> to move to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flinders_Island,_Tasmania" title="Flinders Island, Tasmania">Flinders Island</a>. Many quickly succumbed to infectious diseases to which they had no immunity, reducing the population further.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Of those removed from Tasmania, the last to die was <a href="/wiki/Truganini" title="Truganini">Truganini</a>, in 1876. The near-destruction of Tasmania's Aboriginal population has been described as an act of genocide by historians including <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hughes_(critic)" title="Robert Hughes (critic)">Robert Hughes</a>, James Boyce, Lyndall Ryan and Tom Lawson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes121_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-hughes121-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Boyce has claimed that the April 1828 "Proclamation Separating the Aborigines from the White Inhabitants" sanctioned force against Aboriginals "for no other reason than that they were Aboriginal" and described the decision to remove all Tasmanian Aborigines after 1832—by which time they had given up their fight against white colonists—as an extreme policy position. He concluded: "The colonial government from 1832 to 1838 <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing" title="Ethnic cleansing">ethnically cleansed</a> the western half of Van Diemen's Land and then callously left the exiled people to their fate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Proclamation_as_a_separate_colony">Proclamation as a separate colony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Proclamation as a separate colony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Van Diemen's Land—which thus far had existed as a territory within the colony of <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>—was proclaimed a separate colony, with its own judicial establishment and <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Legislative_Council" title="Tasmanian Legislative Council">Legislative Council</a>, on 3 December 1825. Transportation to the island ceased in 1853 and the colony was renamed Tasmania in 1856, partly to differentiate the burgeoning society of free settlers from the island's convict past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Convict_labourers_in_Australia_in_the_early_20th_century.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="416" data-file-width="672" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Convict_labourers_in_Australia_in_the_early_20th_century.jpg/220px-Convict_labourers_in_Australia_in_the_early_20th_century.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Convict_labourers_in_Australia_in_the_early_20th_century.jpg/330px-Convict_labourers_in_Australia_in_the_early_20th_century.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Convict_labourers_in_Australia_in_the_early_20th_century.jpg/440px-Convict_labourers_in_Australia_in_the_early_20th_century.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Convict_labourers_in_Australia_in_the_early_20th_century.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Convicts_in_Australia" title="Convicts in Australia">convict</a> ploughing team breaking up new ground at the farm at Port Arthur.</div></div></div><p>The <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Legislative_Council" title="Tasmanian Legislative Council">Legislative Council of Van Diemen's Land</a> drafted a new constitution which it passed in 1854. The following year the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privy_Council" title="Privy Council">Privy Council</a> approved the colony changing its name from "Van Diemen's Land" to "Tasmania", and in 1856 the newly elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral_parliament" title="Bicameral parliament">bicameral parliament</a> sat for the first time, establishing Tasmania as a <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">self-governing</a> colony of the British Empire.
</p><p>The colony suffered from economic fluctuations, but for the most part was prosperous, experiencing steady growth. With few external threats and strong trade links with the Empire, Tasmania enjoyed many fruitful periods in the late 19th century, becoming a world-centre of shipbuilding. It raised a local defence force that eventually played a <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Australia_during_the_Second_Boer_War" title="Military history of Australia during the Second Boer War">significant role</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Boer_War" title="Second Boer War">Second Boer War</a> in South Africa, and Tasmanian soldiers in that conflict won the first two <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Cross" title="Victoria Cross">Victoria Crosses</a> awarded to Australians.
</p><p>In 1901 the Colony of Tasmania <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">united</a> with the five other Australian colonies to form the Commonwealth of Australia. Tasmanians voted in favour of federation with the largest majority of all the Australian colonies.
</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Tasmania" title="Colony of Tasmania">Colony of Tasmania</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The state was badly affected by the <a href="/wiki/1967_Tasmanian_fires" title="1967 Tasmanian fires">1967 Tasmanian fires</a>, in which there was major loss of life and property. In the 1970s the state government announced plans to flood environmentally significant <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pedder" title="Lake Pedder">Lake Pedder</a>. As a result of the eventual flooding of Lake Pedder, the world's first greens party was established; the <a href="/wiki/United_Tasmania_Group" title="United Tasmania Group">United Tasmania Group</a>.
</p><p>In 1975 the <a href="/wiki/Tasman_Bridge_disaster" title="Tasman Bridge disaster">Tasman Bridge collapsed</a> when the bridge was struck by the bulk ore carrier <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MV_Lake_Illawarra" title="MV Lake Illawarra">MV Lake Illawarra</a></i>. It was the only bridge in Hobart, and made crossing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Derwent_River_(Tasmania)" title="Derwent River (Tasmania)">Derwent River</a> by road at the city impossible. The nearest bridge was approximately 20 kilometres (12 mi) to the north, at Bridgewater.
</p><p>National and international attention surrounded the campaign against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franklin_Dam" title="Franklin Dam">Franklin Dam</a> in the early 1980s.
</p><p>On 28 April 1996, in the incident now known as the <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur_massacre_(Australia)" title="Port Arthur massacre (Australia)">Port Arthur massacre</a>, lone gunman <a href="/wiki/Martin_Bryant" title="Martin Bryant">Martin Bryant</a> shot and killed 35 people (including tourists and residents) and injured 21 others. The use of <a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">firearms</a> was immediately reviewed, and new gun ownership laws were adopted nationwide, with Tasmania's law one of the strictest in Australia.
</p><p>In April 2006 the <a href="/wiki/Beaconsfield_Mine_collapse" title="Beaconsfield Mine collapse">Beaconsfield Mine collapse</a> was triggered by a small earthquake. One person was killed and two others were trapped underground for 14 days.
</p><p>The Tasmanian community has for some time been divided over the issue of the proposed <a href="/wiki/Bell_Bay_Pulp_Mill" title="Bell Bay Pulp Mill">Bell Bay Pulp Mill</a> to be built in the <a href="/wiki/Tamar_Valley,_Tasmania" title="Tamar Valley, Tasmania">Tamar Valley</a>. Proponents argue that jobs will be created, while opponents argue that pollution will damage both the Bass Strait fishing industry and local tourism. The company behind the proposal collapsed in 2012 and the pulp mill project officially ended in 2017 when the building permits lapsed.
</p><p>In January 2011 philanthropist <a href="/wiki/David_Walsh_(art_collector)" title="David Walsh (art collector)">David Walsh</a> opened the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Old_and_New_Art" title="Museum of Old and New Art">Museum of Old and New Art</a> (MONA) in Hobart to international acclaim. Within 12 months, MONA became Tasmania's top tourism attraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width: -moz-min-content; width: -webkit-min-content; width: min-content; max-width: 100%;"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow: auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Port_Arthur_Panorama.jpg" title="Port Arthur"><img alt="" data-file-height="1782" data-file-width="10971" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Port_Arthur_Panorama.jpg/1540px-Port_Arthur_Panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Port_Arthur_Panorama.jpg/2309px-Port_Arthur_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Port_Arthur_Panorama.jpg/3079px-Port_Arthur_Panorama.jpg 2x" width="1540"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_Arthur_Panorama.jpg" title="File:Port Arthur Panorama.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur,_Tasmania" title="Port Arthur, Tasmania">Port Arthur</a></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Topography_of_Tasmania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1237" decoding="async" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Topography_of_Tasmania.jpg/220px-Topography_of_Tasmania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Topography_of_Tasmania.jpg/330px-Topography_of_Tasmania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Topography_of_Tasmania.jpg/440px-Topography_of_Tasmania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Topography_of_Tasmania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topography of Tasmania</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Bridestowe_Estate,_Tasmania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/The_Bridestowe_Estate%2C_Tasmania.jpg/220px-The_Bridestowe_Estate%2C_Tasmania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/The_Bridestowe_Estate%2C_Tasmania.jpg/330px-The_Bridestowe_Estate%2C_Tasmania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/The_Bridestowe_Estate%2C_Tasmania.jpg/440px-The_Bridestowe_Estate%2C_Tasmania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Bridestowe_Estate,_Tasmania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A lavender farm in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nabowla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nabowla (page does not exist)">Nabowla</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cradle_Mountain_Behind_Dove_Lake.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Cradle_Mountain_Behind_Dove_Lake.jpg/220px-Cradle_Mountain_Behind_Dove_Lake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Cradle_Mountain_Behind_Dove_Lake.jpg/330px-Cradle_Mountain_Behind_Dove_Lake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Cradle_Mountain_Behind_Dove_Lake.jpg/440px-Cradle_Mountain_Behind_Dove_Lake.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cradle_Mountain_Behind_Dove_Lake.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dove_Lake_(Tasmania)" title="Dove Lake (Tasmania)">Dove Lake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cradle_Mountain" title="Cradle Mountain">Cradle Mountain</a>, Central Tasmanian Highlands</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:North_Coast_of_Tasmania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1165" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/North_Coast_of_Tasmania.jpg/220px-North_Coast_of_Tasmania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/North_Coast_of_Tasmania.jpg/330px-North_Coast_of_Tasmania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/North_Coast_of_Tasmania.jpg/440px-North_Coast_of_Tasmania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:North_Coast_of_Tasmania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>North Coast of Tasmania</div></div></div>
<p>Tasmania's landmass of 68,401 km<sup>2</sup> (26,410 sq mi) is located directly in the pathway of the notorious "<a href="/wiki/Roaring_Forties" title="Roaring Forties">Roaring Forties</a>" wind that encircles the globe. To its north, it is separated from mainland Australia by <a href="/wiki/Bass_Strait" title="Bass Strait">Bass Strait</a>. Tasmania is the only Australian state that is not located on the Australian mainland. About 2,500 kilometres (1,600 mi) south of Tasmania island lies <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>. Tasmania is in fact geographically closer to Antarctica than it is to parts of the northern Australian mainland.
</p><p>Depending on which <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_the_oceans" title="Borders of the oceans">borders of the oceans</a> are used, the island can be said to be either surrounded by the Southern Ocean, or to have the Pacific on its east and the Indian to its west. Still other definitions of the ocean boundaries would have Tasmania with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Australian_Bight" title="Great Australian Bight">Great Australian Bight</a> to the west, and the <a href="/wiki/Tasman_Sea" title="Tasman Sea">Tasman Sea</a> to the east. It lies at similar latitudes to the <a href="/wiki/South_Island" title="South Island">South Island</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, and parts of <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.
</p><p>Tasmania has been volcanically inactive in recent geological times but has many jagged peaks resulting from recent <a href="/wiki/Glacial_period" title="Glacial period">glaciation</a>. Tasmania is the most mountainous state in Australia. The most mountainous region is the <a href="/wiki/Central_Highlands_(Tasmania)" title="Central Highlands (Tasmania)">Central Highlands</a> area, which covers most of the central western parts of the state. The <a href="/wiki/Midlands_(Tasmania)" title="Midlands (Tasmania)">Midlands</a> located in the central east, is fairly flat, and is predominantly used for agriculture, although farming activity is scattered throughout the state. Tasmania's tallest mountain is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Ossa_(Tasmania)" title="Mount Ossa (Tasmania)">Mount Ossa</a> at 1,617 m (5,305 ft). The mountain lies in the heart of the world-famous <a href="/wiki/Cradle_Mountain-Lake_St_Clair_National_Park" title="Cradle Mountain-Lake St Clair National Park">Cradle Mountain-Lake St Clair National Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-height_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-height-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Much of Tasmania is still densely forested, with the <a href="/wiki/Southwest_National_Park" title="Southwest National Park">Southwest National Park</a> and neighbouring areas holding some of the last temperate rain forests in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Tarkine" title="Tarkine">Tarkine</a>, containing <a href="/wiki/Savage_River_National_Park" title="Savage River National Park">Savage River National Park</a> located in the island's far north west, is the largest <a href="/wiki/Temperate_rainforest" title="Temperate rainforest">temperate rainforest</a> area in Australia covering about 3,800 square kilometres (1,500 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>
With its rugged topography, Tasmania has a great number of rivers. Several of Tasmania's largest rivers have been dammed at some point to provide <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a>. Many rivers begin in the Central Highlands and flow out to the coast. Tasmania's major population centres are mainly situated around <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estuaries" title="Estuaries">estuaries</a> (some of which are named rivers).
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Derwent_River_(Tasmania)" title="Derwent River (Tasmania)">Derwent River</a> flows south east and reaches the coast at Hobart; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamar_River" title="Tamar River">Tamar River</a> flows north from Launceston; the <a href="/wiki/Mersey_River_(Tasmania)" title="Mersey River (Tasmania)">Mersey River</a> also flows north to the North West Coast at Devonport; the Franklin and Gordon Rivers flow west and meet the coast at <a href="/wiki/Strahan,_Tasmania" title="Strahan, Tasmania">Strahan</a>. The <a href="/wiki/South_Esk_River" title="South Esk River">South Esk River</a> is the longest river in Tasmania. It starts in the mountains at <a href="/wiki/Fingal" title="Fingal">Fingal</a> and flows through <a href="/wiki/Avoca,_Tasmania" title="Avoca, Tasmania">Avoca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evandale,_Tasmania" title="Evandale, Tasmania">Evandale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Longford,_Tasmania" title="Longford, Tasmania">Longford</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hadspen" title="Hadspen">Hadspen</a> and finally Launceston. The river is dammed at Launceston's <a href="/wiki/Trevallyn_Dam" title="Trevallyn Dam">Trevallyn Dam</a> and used for the city's <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a>. Although most of the water is dammed at Lake Trevallyn, some flows on into the <a href="/wiki/Cataract_Gorge" title="Cataract Gorge">Cataract Gorge</a>, where it becomes a tributary to the Tamar Estuary, and the outflow from the power station also joins the Tamar River downstream of Launceston.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>The state of Tasmania shares a land border with <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> at its northernmost terrestrial point, <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Islet" title="Boundary Islet">Boundary Islet</a>, a nature reserve in Bass Strait.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The existence of the 85 m (280 ft) land border is an administrative quirk caused by an early mapping error. Tasmania also includes <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Island" title="Macquarie Island">Macquarie Island</a>, situated 1,500 km (930 mi) south of the state, and approximately halfway between <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctic mainland</a>, along with neighbouring island groups <a href="/wiki/Judge_and_Clerk_Islets" title="Judge and Clerk Islets">Judge and Clerk Islets</a> 11 km (7 mi) north and <a href="/wiki/Bishop_and_Clerk_Islets" title="Bishop and Clerk Islets">Bishop and Clerk Islets</a> about 37 km (23 mi) south of Macquarie Island. The latter include the southernmost terrestrial point of the state of Tasmania, and the southernmost internationally recognised land in Australia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:auto; max-width:858px;">
<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wineglass_Bay_seen_from_Mount_Amos_at_Freycinet_National_Park_(Tasmania).jpg" title="Wineglass Bay seen from Mount Amos at Freycinet National Park"><img alt="" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="12416" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wineglass_Bay_seen_from_Mount_Amos_at_Freycinet_National_Park_%28Tasmania%29.jpg/850px-Wineglass_Bay_seen_from_Mount_Amos_at_Freycinet_National_Park_%28Tasmania%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wineglass_Bay_seen_from_Mount_Amos_at_Freycinet_National_Park_%28Tasmania%29.jpg/1275px-Wineglass_Bay_seen_from_Mount_Amos_at_Freycinet_National_Park_%28Tasmania%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wineglass_Bay_seen_from_Mount_Amos_at_Freycinet_National_Park_%28Tasmania%29.jpg/1700px-Wineglass_Bay_seen_from_Mount_Amos_at_Freycinet_National_Park_%28Tasmania%29.jpg 2x" width="850"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wineglass_Bay_seen_from_Mount_Amos_at_Freycinet_National_Park_(Tasmania).jpg" title="File:Wineglass Bay seen from Mount Amos at Freycinet National Park (Tasmania).jpg"> </a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wineglass_Bay" title="Wineglass Bay">Wineglass Bay</a> seen from Mount Amos at <a href="/wiki/Freycinet_National_Park" title="Freycinet National Park">Freycinet National Park</a></div>
</div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Insularity">Insularity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Insularity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tasmania's insularity was probably detected by Captain <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> when he charted Tasmania's coast in 1642. On 5 December, Tasman was following the east coast northward to see how far it went. When the land veered to the north-west at <a href="/wiki/Eddystone_Point" title="Eddystone Point">Eddystone Point</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> he tried to keep in with it but his ships were suddenly hit by the <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Forties" title="Roaring Forties">Roaring Forties</a> howling through Banks Strait.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Tasman was on a mission to find the Southern Continent, not more islands, so he abruptly turned away to the east and continued his continent-hunting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>The next European to enter the strait was Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> in the <i>Endeavour</i> in April 1770. A talented and diligent hydrographer, Cook quickly identified the strait, but knew he had to conceal it. The <a href="/wiki/Admiralty" title="Admiralty">Admiralty</a> had issued its usual instructions to hide strategically important discoveries that could become security risks, such as off-shore islands from which operations could be mounted by a hostile power, at a time of intense <a href="/wiki/France%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="France–United Kingdom relations">Anglo-French rivalry</a>.
</p><p>Consequently, in his journal Cook disguised his discovery with a riddle;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and on his chart he drew a curtain across the truncated channel by sketching a false coastline down to an invented <a href="/wiki/Point_Hicks" title="Point Hicks">Point Hicks</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Cook's ploy worked and Tasmania's insularity was suppressed for three more decades, as Europe's mapmakers increasingly depicted it as a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> joined to the mainland.
</p><p>The age-old question about Tasmania's insularity – 'Is Van Diemen's Land a peninsula or an island?' – was officially resolved in 1798–99 when George Bass and Matthew Flinders circumnavigated the island. When news of their discovery of Bass Strait reached Europe, the French government despatched a reconnaissance expedition commanded by <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Baudin" title="Nicolas Baudin">Nicolas Baudin</a>. This prompted <a href="/wiki/Philip_Gidley_King" title="Philip Gidley King">Governor King</a> to send two vessels from Sydney to the island to establish a garrison at Hobart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Tasmania" title="Climate of Tasmania">Climate of Tasmania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Knyvet_Falls,_Tasmania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="885" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Knyvet_Falls%2C_Tasmania.jpg/220px-Knyvet_Falls%2C_Tasmania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Knyvet_Falls%2C_Tasmania.jpg/330px-Knyvet_Falls%2C_Tasmania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Knyvet_Falls%2C_Tasmania.jpg/440px-Knyvet_Falls%2C_Tasmania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Knyvet_Falls,_Tasmania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Knyvet Falls near Cradle Mountain, Tasmania</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blick_ueber_Great_Oyster_Bay_zur_Freycinet_Peninsula.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="499" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Blick_ueber_Great_Oyster_Bay_zur_Freycinet_Peninsula.jpg/220px-Blick_ueber_Great_Oyster_Bay_zur_Freycinet_Peninsula.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Blick_ueber_Great_Oyster_Bay_zur_Freycinet_Peninsula.jpg/330px-Blick_ueber_Great_Oyster_Bay_zur_Freycinet_Peninsula.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Blick_ueber_Great_Oyster_Bay_zur_Freycinet_Peninsula.jpg/440px-Blick_ueber_Great_Oyster_Bay_zur_Freycinet_Peninsula.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blick_ueber_Great_Oyster_Bay_zur_Freycinet_Peninsula.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Moulting_Lagoon_Important_Bird_Area" title="Moulting Lagoon Important Bird Area">Moulting Lagoon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Oyster_Bay" title="Great Oyster Bay">Great Oyster Bay</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Freycinet_Peninsula" title="Freycinet Peninsula">Freycinet Peninsula</a> in the distance</div></div></div>
<p>Tasmania has a relatively cool temperate climate compared to the rest of Australia with four distinct seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Summer is from December to February when the average maximum sea temperature is 21 °C (70 °F) and inland areas around Launceston reach 24 °C (75 °F). Other inland areas are much cooler, with <a href="/wiki/Liawenee" title="Liawenee">Liawenee</a>, located on the Central Plateau, one of the coldest places in Australia, ranging between 4 °C (39 °F) and 17 °C (63 °F) in February. Autumn is from March to May, with mostly settled weather, as summer patterns gradually take on the shape of winter patterns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The winter months are from June to August, and are generally the wettest and coolest months in the state, with most high lying areas receiving considerable snowfall. Winter maximums are 12 °C (54 °F) on average along coastal areas and 3 °C (37 °F) on the central plateau, as a result of a series of cold fronts from the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a>. Inland areas receive regular freezes throughout the winter months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Spring is from September to November, and is an unsettled season of transition, where winter weather patterns begin to take the shape of summer patterns, although snowfall is still common up until October. Spring is generally the windiest time of the year with afternoon sea breezes starting to take effect on the coast.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soils">Soils</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Soils">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apple_orchard_in_Tasmania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Apple_orchard_in_Tasmania.jpg/220px-Apple_orchard_in_Tasmania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Apple_orchard_in_Tasmania.jpg/330px-Apple_orchard_in_Tasmania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Apple_orchard_in_Tasmania.jpg/440px-Apple_orchard_in_Tasmania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apple_orchard_in_Tasmania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An apple orchard in the "Apple Isle".</div></div></div>
<p>Despite the presence of some <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glaciation" title="Glaciation">glaciation</a>, Tasmania's soils are not more fertile than those of mainland Australia, largely because most are severely <a href="/wiki/Leaching_(agriculture)" title="Leaching (agriculture)">leached</a> and the areas with driest climates (least leaching) were unaffected by glaciation or alluvia derived therefrom. Most soils on the Bass Strait Islands, the east coast and western Tasmania are very infertile <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spodosols" title="Spodosols">spodosols</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psamments" title="Psamments">psamments</a>, with some even less fertile "lateritic podzolic soils" in the latter region. Most of these lands are thus not used for agriculture, but there is much productive forestry—which remains one of the state's major industries.
</p><p>On the north coast, apart from some relatively fertile alluvial soils used for fruit-growing, there are also deep red, easily workable soils known as "krasnozems" ("red land"). These soils are highly acidic and fix phosphate very effectively, but their extremely favourable physical properties make them extensively used for dairying, beef cattle and fodder crops.
</p><p>The Midlands and the Lower Derwent present a different story from the rest of the state. Owing to a relatively dry climate and alkaline (mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dolerite" title="Dolerite">dolerite</a>) parent material, these soils are relatively unleached and contain lime in the deeper subsoil. They are mostly classified as "prairie soils" or "brown earths" and bear some resemblance to the <a href="/wiki/Chernozem" title="Chernozem">chernozems</a> of Russia and North America, although they are much lower in available <a href="/wiki/Phosphorus" title="Phosphorus">phosphorus</a> and somewhat acidic in the surface levels. Their higher nutrient levels, however, allow them to support productive pasture, and large numbers of sheep are grazed in these regions. Some grain crops are also grown in the driest areas. In the alluvial areas of southeastern Tasmania, rich alluvial soils permit apples to be grown.
</p><p>Tasmania became known as the "Apple Isle" because for many years it was one of the world's major apple producers. Apples are still grown in large numbers, particularly in southern Tasmania, and have the distinction of being the first approved by the Japanese government for import, due to their verifiable pest-free status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Why_is_Tasmania_called_the_'Apple_Isle'_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Why_is_Tasmania_called_the_'Apple_Isle'-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flora_and_fauna_of_Tasmania" title="Flora and fauna of Tasmania">Flora and fauna of Tasmania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hellyer_Gorge,_Tasmania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hellyer_Gorge%2C_Tasmania.jpg/220px-Hellyer_Gorge%2C_Tasmania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hellyer_Gorge%2C_Tasmania.jpg/330px-Hellyer_Gorge%2C_Tasmania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hellyer_Gorge%2C_Tasmania.jpg/440px-Hellyer_Gorge%2C_Tasmania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hellyer_Gorge,_Tasmania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">Ferns</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hellyer_Gorge" title="Hellyer Gorge">Hellyer Gorge</a>, to the northeast of <a href="/wiki/Savage_River_National_Park" title="Savage River National Park">Savage River National Park</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tasmanian_Devil_resting.jpg"><img alt="A devil lying belly down on dry scrub grass and dead leaves. It has stretched its front legs out in front of its face." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1488" data-file-width="2240" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Tasmanian_Devil_resting.jpg/220px-Tasmanian_Devil_resting.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Tasmanian_Devil_resting.jpg/330px-Tasmanian_Devil_resting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Tasmanian_Devil_resting.jpg/440px-Tasmanian_Devil_resting.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tasmanian_Devil_resting.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Although <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_devil" title="Tasmanian devil">Tasmanian devils</a> are nocturnal, they like to rest in the sun. <a href="/wiki/Scar" title="Scar">Scarring</a> from fighting is visible next to this devil's left eye.</div></div></div>
<p>Geographically and genetically isolated, Tasmania is known for its unique flora and fauna. 
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Tasmania has <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">extremely diverse</a> vegetation, from the heavily grazed grassland of the dry Midlands to the tall evergreen <a href="/wiki/Eucalypt" title="Eucalypt">eucalypt</a> forest, <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine</a> heathlands and large areas of cool <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate_rain_forest" title="Temperate rain forest">temperate rainforests</a> and moorlands in the rest of the state. Many flora species are unique to Tasmania, and some are related to species in South America and New Zealand through ancestors which grew on the super continent of <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwana</a>, 50 million years ago.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The island of Tasmania was home to the <a href="/wiki/Thylacine" title="Thylacine">thylacine</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Marsupial" title="Marsupial">marsupial</a> which resembled a <a href="/wiki/Fossa_(animal)" title="Fossa (animal)">fossa</a> or some say a wild dog. Known colloquially as the Tasmanian tiger for the distinctive striping across its back, it became extinct in mainland Australia much earlier because of competition by the <a href="/wiki/Dingo" title="Dingo">dingo</a>, introduced in prehistoric times. Owing to persecution by farmers, government-funded bounty hunters and, in the final years, collectors for overseas museums, it appears to have been exterminated in Tasmania. The <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_devil" title="Tasmanian devil">Tasmanian devil</a> became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_mammals#Marsupials_(Marsupialia)" title="Largest mammals">largest carnivorous marsupial</a> in the world following the <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Thylacine" title="Thylacine">thylacine</a> in 1936, and is now found in the wild only in Tasmania. Tasmania was one of the last regions of Australia to be introduced to domesticated dogs. Dogs were brought from Britain in 1803 for hunting kangaroos and emus. This introduction completely transformed Aboriginal society, as it helped them to successfully compete with European hunters, and was more important than the introduction of guns for the Aboriginals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hobart_moonrise_from_Mt_Wellington.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Hobart_moonrise_from_Mt_Wellington.jpg/220px-Hobart_moonrise_from_Mt_Wellington.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Hobart_moonrise_from_Mt_Wellington.jpg/330px-Hobart_moonrise_from_Mt_Wellington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Hobart_moonrise_from_Mt_Wellington.jpg/440px-Hobart_moonrise_from_Mt_Wellington.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hobart_moonrise_from_Mt_Wellington.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The city of <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a>, seen here from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Wellington,_Tasmania" title="Mount Wellington, Tasmania">Mount Wellington</a>, is Tasmania's most populous city and comprises a large portion of the state's population.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ABS-3101.0-AustralianDemographicStatistics-EstimatedResidentPopulationStatesTerritories-EstimatedResidentPopulation-Persons-Tasmania-A2060848V.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="341" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ABS-3101.0-AustralianDemographicStatistics-EstimatedResidentPopulationStatesTerritories-EstimatedResidentPopulation-Persons-Tasmania-A2060848V.svg/220px-ABS-3101.0-AustralianDemographicStatistics-EstimatedResidentPopulationStatesTerritories-EstimatedResidentPopulation-Persons-Tasmania-A2060848V.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ABS-3101.0-AustralianDemographicStatistics-EstimatedResidentPopulationStatesTerritories-EstimatedResidentPopulation-Persons-Tasmania-A2060848V.svg/330px-ABS-3101.0-AustralianDemographicStatistics-EstimatedResidentPopulationStatesTerritories-EstimatedResidentPopulation-Persons-Tasmania-A2060848V.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ABS-3101.0-AustralianDemographicStatistics-EstimatedResidentPopulationStatesTerritories-EstimatedResidentPopulation-Persons-Tasmania-A2060848V.svg/440px-ABS-3101.0-AustralianDemographicStatistics-EstimatedResidentPopulationStatesTerritories-EstimatedResidentPopulation-Persons-Tasmania-A2060848V.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ABS-3101.0-AustralianDemographicStatistics-EstimatedResidentPopulationStatesTerritories-EstimatedResidentPopulation-Persons-Tasmania-A2060848V.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estimated resident population since 1981</div></div></div>
<p>Tasmania's population is more homogeneous than that of other states of Australia, with many of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a> descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Approximately 65% of its residents are descendants of an estimated 10,000 "founding families" from the mid-19th century. As of  1996<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, more than 80% of Tasmanians were born in the state and almost 90% were born in Australia, New Zealand, Great Britain, or Ireland.
</p><p>Until 2012, Tasmania was the only state in Australia with an above-replacement <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a>; Tasmanian women had an average of 2.24 children each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> By 2012 the birth rate had slipped to 2.1 children per woman, bringing the state to the replacement threshold, but it continues to have the second-highest birth rate of any state or territory (behind the Northern Territory).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Major population centres include <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Launceston,_Tasmania" title="Launceston, Tasmania">Launceston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Devonport,_Tasmania" title="Devonport, Tasmania">Devonport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burnie,_Tasmania" title="Burnie, Tasmania">Burnie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ulverstone,_Tasmania" title="Ulverstone, Tasmania">Ulverstone</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Tasmania" title="Kingston, Tasmania">Kingston</a> is often defined as a separate city but is generally regarded as part of the Greater Hobart Area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs a reliable source; Kingston is often defined as a separate city but is generally regarded as part of the Greater Hobart Area. (August 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
