<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Tasmania" title="Government of Tasmania">Government of Tasmania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CG-ParliamentHouseHobart.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="76" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/CG-ParliamentHouseHobart.jpg/220px-CG-ParliamentHouseHobart.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/CG-ParliamentHouseHobart.jpg/330px-CG-ParliamentHouseHobart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/CG-ParliamentHouseHobart.jpg/440px-CG-ParliamentHouseHobart.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CG-ParliamentHouseHobart.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Hobart" title="Parliament House, Hobart">Parliament House, Hobart</a></div></div></div>
<p>The form of the government of Tasmania is prescribed in its constitution, which dates from 1856, although it has been amended many times since then. Since 1901, Tasmania has been a state of the Commonwealth of Australia, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Constitution" title="Australian Constitution">Australian Constitution</a> regulates its relationship with the Commonwealth and prescribes which powers each level of government is allowed.
</p>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Tasmania" title="List of Governors of Tasmania">Governors of Tasmania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Tasmania" title="Parliament of Tasmania">Parliament of Tasmania</a></div>
<p>Tasmania is a State in the Australian federation. Its relationship with the Federal Government and Parliament are regulated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Constitution" title="Australian Constitution">Australian Constitution</a>. Tasmania is represented in the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Senate" title="Australian Senate">Senate</a> by 12 senators, on an equal basis with all other states. In the <a href="/wiki/Australian_House_of_Representatives" title="Australian House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>, Tasmania is entitled to five seats, which is the minimum allocation for a state guaranteed by the Constitution—the number of House of Representatives seats for each state is otherwise decided on the basis of their relative populations, and Tasmania has never qualified for five seats on that basis alone. Tasmania's <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_House_of_Assembly" title="Tasmanian House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a> use a system of multi-seat <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_Transferable_Vote" title="Single Transferable Vote">Hare-Clark</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_state_election,_2002" title="Tasmanian state election, 2002">2002 state election</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Labor Party</a> won 14 of the 25 House seats. The people decreased their vote for the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Australia" title="Liberal Party of Australia">Liberal Party</a>; representation in the Parliament fell to seven seats. The <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Greens" title="Tasmanian Greens">Greens</a> won four seats, with over 18% of the popular vote, the highest proportion of any Green party in any parliament in the world at that time.
</p>

<p>On 23 February 2004 the Premier <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bacon" title="Jim Bacon">Jim Bacon</a> announced his retirement, after being diagnosed with lung cancer. In his last months he opened a vigorous anti-smoking campaign which included many restrictions on where individuals could smoke, such as pubs. He died four months later. Bacon was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lennon" title="Paul Lennon">Paul Lennon</a>, who, after leading the state for two years, went on to win the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_state_election,_2006" title="Tasmanian state election, 2006">2006 state election</a> in his own right. Lennon resigned in 2008 and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/David_Bartlett" title="David Bartlett">David Bartlett</a>, who formed a coalition government with the Greens after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_state_election,_2010" title="Tasmanian state election, 2010">2010 state election</a> resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Hung_parliament" title="Hung parliament">hung parliament</a>. Bartlett resigned as Premier in January 2011 and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Lara_Giddings" title="Lara Giddings">Lara Giddings</a>, who became Tasmania's first female Premier.  In March 2014 <a href="/wiki/Will_Hodgman" title="Will Hodgman">Will Hodgman</a>'s Liberal Party won government, ending sixteen years of Labor governance, and ending an eight-year period for Hodgman himself as <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Tasmania)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Tasmania)">Leader of the Opposition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Hodgman then won a second term of government in the recent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_state_election,_2018" title="Tasmanian state election, 2018">2018 state election</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tasmania has a number of undeveloped regions. Proposals for local economic development have been faced with requirements for environmental sensitivity, or opposition. In particular, proposals for hydroelectric power generation were debated in the late 20th century. In the 1970s, opposition to the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pedder" title="Lake Pedder">Lake Pedder</a> reservoir impoundment led to the formation of the world's first <a href="/wiki/Green_party" title="Green party">green party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Tasmania_Group" title="United Tasmania Group">United Tasmania Group</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lake_Pedder_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lake_Pedder-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lake_Pedder_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lake_Pedder-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 1980s the state debated the proposed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franklin_Dam" title="Franklin Dam">Franklin River Dam</a>. The anti-dam sentiment was shared by many Australians outside Tasmania and proved a factor in the election of the <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hawke" title="Bob Hawke">Hawke</a> <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Labor</a> government in 1983, which halted construction of the dam. Since the 1980s the environmental focus has shifted to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_growth" title="Old growth">old growth</a> logging and mining in the Tarkine region, which have both proved divisive. The Tasmania Together process recommended an end to clear felling in high conservation old growth forests by January 2003, but was unsuccessful.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tasmania has 29 <a href="/wiki/Local_government_areas_of_Tasmania" title="Local government areas of Tasmania">local government areas</a>. Local councils are responsible for functions delegated by the Tasmanian parliament, such as urban planning, road infrastructure and waste management. Council revenue comes mostly from property taxes and government grants.
</p><p>As with the <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_House_of_Assembly" title="Tasmanian House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a>, Tasmania's local government elections use a system of multi-seat <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Single_transferable_vote" title="Single transferable vote">Hare–Clark</a>. Local government elections take place every four years and are conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Electoral_Commission" title="Tasmanian Electoral Commission">Tasmanian Electoral Commission</a> by full <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postal_ballot" title="Postal ballot">postal ballot</a>. The next local government elections will be held during September and October 2018.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Tasmania" title="Economy of Tasmania">Economy of Tasmania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WesternTasmania1865.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1534" data-file-width="1248" decoding="async" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/WesternTasmania1865.jpg/220px-WesternTasmania1865.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/WesternTasmania1865.jpg/330px-WesternTasmania1865.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/WesternTasmania1865.jpg/440px-WesternTasmania1865.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WesternTasmania1865.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/West_Coast,_Tasmania" title="West Coast, Tasmania">Western Tasmania</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_West_Tasmania" title="South West Tasmania">South West Tasmania</a> with natural resources on 1865 map</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tasmanian_salmon_on_a_pea_and_corn_fritter.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1371" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Tasmanian_salmon_on_a_pea_and_corn_fritter.jpg/220px-Tasmanian_salmon_on_a_pea_and_corn_fritter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Tasmanian_salmon_on_a_pea_and_corn_fritter.jpg/330px-Tasmanian_salmon_on_a_pea_and_corn_fritter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Tasmanian_salmon_on_a_pea_and_corn_fritter.jpg/440px-Tasmanian_salmon_on_a_pea_and_corn_fritter.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tasmanian_salmon_on_a_pea_and_corn_fritter.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Smoked Tasmanian salmon. Tasmania is a large exporter of seafood, particularly <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Traditionally, Tasmania's main industries have been mining (including copper, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, and iron), agriculture, forestry, and tourism. In the 1940s and 1950s, a hydro-industrialisation initiative was embodied in the state by <a href="/wiki/Hydro_Tasmania" title="Hydro Tasmania">Hydro Tasmania</a>. These all have had varying fortunes over the last century and more, involved in ebbs and flows of population moving in and away dependent upon the specific requirements of the dominant industries of the time. The state also has a large number of food exporting sectors, including but not limited to seafood (such as <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_salmon" title="Atlantic salmon">Atlantic salmon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abalone" title="Abalone">abalone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crayfish" title="Crayfish">crayfish</a>).
</p><p>In the 1960s and 1970s there was a decline in traditional crops such as apples and pears,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> with other crops and industries eventually rising in their place. During the 15 years until 2010, new agricultural products such as wine, <a href="/wiki/Saffron" title="Saffron">saffron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyrethrum" title="Pyrethrum">pyrethrum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cherry" title="Cherry">cherries</a> have been fostered by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Institute_of_Agricultural_Research" title="Tasmanian Institute of Agricultural Research">Tasmanian Institute of Agricultural Research</a>.
</p><p>Favourable economic conditions throughout Australia, cheaper air fares, and two new <i>Spirit of Tasmania</i> ferries have all contributed to what is now a rising tourism industry.
</p><p>About 1.7% of the Tasmanian population are employed by local government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Other major employers include <a href="/wiki/Nyrstar" title="Nyrstar">Nyrstar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norske_Skog" title="Norske Skog">Norske Skog</a>, Grange Resources, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Group" title="Rio Tinto Group">Rio Tinto</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Hobart" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Hobart">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Hobart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Federal_Group" title="Federal Group">Federal Group</a>. Small business is a large part of the community life, including <a href="/wiki/Incat" title="Incat">Incat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moorilla_Estate" title="Moorilla Estate">Moorilla Estate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tassal" title="Tassal">Tassal</a>. In the late 1990s, a number of national companies based their call centres in the state after obtaining cheap access to broad-band fibre optic connections.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>34% of Tasmanians are reliant on welfare payments as their primary source of income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> This number is in part due to the large number of older residents and retirees in Tasmania receiving Age Pensions. Due to its natural environment and clean air, Tasmania is a common retirement selection for Australians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_wine" title="Tasmanian wine">Tasmanian wine</a></div>
<p>During colonial times the cuisines of the British Isles were the standard in most areas of Tasmania. Tasmania now has a wide range of restaurants, in part due to the arrival of immigrants and changing cultural patterns. Scattered across Tasmania are many vineyards,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goway_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-goway-75">[75]</a></sup> and Tasmanian beer brands such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boags" title="Boags">Boags</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Brewery" title="Cascade Brewery">Cascade</a> are known and sold in Mainland Australia. <a href="/wiki/King_Island_(Tasmania)" title="King Island (Tasmania)">King Island</a> off the northwestern coast of Tasmania has a reputation for boutique cheeses<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goway_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-goway-75">[75]</a></sup> and dairy products. Tasmanians are also consumers of seafood,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goway_75-2"><a href="#cite_note-goway-75">[75]</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Crayfish" title="Crayfish">crayfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_roughy" title="Orange roughy">orange roughy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salmon_(food)" title="Salmon (food)">salmon</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goway_75-3"><a href="#cite_note-goway-75">[75]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Oyster" title="Oyster">oysters</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goway_75-4"><a href="#cite_note-goway-75">[75]</a></sup> both farmed and wild.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_events_in_Tasmania" title="List of events in Tasmania">List of events in Tasmania</a></div>
<p>To foster tourism, the state government encourages or supports several annual events in and around the island. The best known of these is the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_to_Hobart_Yacht_Race" title="Sydney to Hobart Yacht Race">Sydney to Hobart Yacht Race</a>, starting on <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a> in Sydney and usually arriving at <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Dock" title="Constitution Dock">Constitution Dock</a> in Hobart around three to four days later, during the <a href="/wiki/Taste_of_Tasmania" title="Taste of Tasmania">Taste of Tasmania</a>, an annual food and wine festival. Other events include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rally_racing" title="Rally racing">road rally</a> <a href="/wiki/Targa_Tasmania" title="Targa Tasmania">Targa Tasmania</a> which attracts rally drivers from around the world and is staged all over the state, over five days. Rural or regional events include <a href="/wiki/Agfest" title="Agfest">Agfest</a>, a three-day <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_show" title="Agricultural show">agricultural show</a> held at <a href="/wiki/Carrick,_Tasmania" title="Carrick, Tasmania">Carrick</a> (just west of Launceston) in early May and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hobart_Show" title="Royal Hobart Show">Royal Hobart Show</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Launceston_Show" title="Royal Launceston Show">Royal Launceston Show</a>, both held in October annually. Music events held in Tasmania include the <a href="/wiki/Falls_Festival" title="Falls Festival">Falls Festival</a> at <a href="/wiki/Marion_Bay,_Tasmania" title="Marion Bay, Tasmania">Marion Bay</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victorian</a> event now held in both Victoria and Tasmania on New Year's Eve), the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Festival_of_Voices&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Festival of Voices (page does not exist)">Festival of Voices</a>, a national celebration of song held each year in Hobart attracting international and national teachers and choirs in the heart of Winter, <a href="/wiki/MS_Fest" title="MS Fest">MS Fest</a> is a charity music event held in Launceston, to raise money for those with <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a>. The Cygnet Folk Festival is one Australia's most iconic folk music festivals and is held every year in January, the Tasmanian Lute Festival is an early music event held in different locations in Tasmania every two years. Recent additions to the state arts events calendar include the <a href="/wiki/10_Days_on_the_Island" title="10 Days on the Island">10 Days on the Island</a> arts festival, <a href="/wiki/MONA_FOMA" title="MONA FOMA">MONA FOMA</a>, run by <a href="/wiki/David_Walsh_(art_collector)" title="David Walsh (art collector)">David Walsh</a> and curated by <a href="/wiki/Brian_Ritchie" title="Brian Ritchie">Brian Ritchie</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dark_MOFO&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dark MOFO (page does not exist)">Dark MOFO</a> also run by <a href="/wiki/David_Walsh_(art_collector)" title="David Walsh (art collector)">David Walsh</a> and curated by Leigh Carmichael.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_literature" title="Tasmanian literature">Tasmanian literature</a></div>
<p>Notable titles by Tasmanian authors include <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/For_the_Term_of_his_Natural_Life" title="For the Term of his Natural Life">For the Term of his Natural Life</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Clarke" title="Marcus Clarke">Marcus Clarke</a>, <i>The Museum of Modern Love</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Heather_Rose" title="Heather Rose">Heather Rose</a>, <i>The Narrow Road to the Deep North</i> by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Flanagan" title="Richard Flanagan">Richard Flanagan</a>, <i>The Alphabet of Light and Dark</i> by <a href="/wiki/Danielle_Wood" title="Danielle Wood">Danielle Wood</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Roving_Party" title="The Roving Party">The Roving Party</a></i> by Rohan Wilson and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Year_of_Living_Dangerously_(novel)" title="The Year of Living Dangerously (novel)">The Year of Living Dangerously</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Koch" title="Christopher Koch">Christopher Koch</a>, <i>The Rain Queen</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Scholes" title="Katherine Scholes">Katherine Scholes</a>, <i>Bridget Crack</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> by Rachel Leary, and <i>The Blue Day Book</i> by <a href="/wiki/Bradley_Trevor_Greive" title="Bradley Trevor Greive">Bradley Trevor Greive</a>. Children's books include <i>They Found a Cave</i> by <a href="/wiki/Nan_Chauncy" title="Nan Chauncy">Nan Chauncy</a>, <i>The Museum of Thieves</i> by <a href="/wiki/Lian_Tanner" title="Lian Tanner">Lian Tanner</a>, <i>Finding Serendipity</i>, <i>A Week Without Tuesday</i> and <i>Blueberry Pancakes Forever</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> by Angelica Banks, <i><a href="/wiki/Tiger_Tale" title="Tiger Tale">Tiger Tale</a></i> by Marion and Steve Isham. Tasmania is home to the eminent literary magazine that was formed in 1979, <a href="/wiki/Island_magazine" title="Island magazine">Island magazine</a>, and the biennial Tasmanian Writers and Readers Festival.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Media" title="Tasmanian Media">Tasmanian Media</a></div>
<p>Tasmania has five broadcast television stations which produce local content including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_Tasmania" title="ABC Tasmania">ABC Tasmania</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Cross_Television" title="Southern Cross Television">Seven Tasmania</a> – an affiliate of <a href="/wiki/Seven_Network" title="Seven Network">Seven Network</a>, <a href="/wiki/WIN_Television" title="WIN Television">WIN Television Tasmania</a> – an affiliate of <a href="/wiki/Network_Ten" title="Network Ten">Ten Network</a>, Nine Tasmania – an affiliate of the <a href="/wiki/Nine_Network" title="Nine Network">Nine Network</a> (joint owned by WIN and Southern Cross), and <a href="/wiki/Special_Broadcasting_Service" title="Special Broadcasting Service">SBS</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_performing_arts">Music and performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Music and performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Theatre_at_night,_Launceston.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1950" data-file-width="2600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Princess_Theatre_at_night%2C_Launceston.JPG/220px-Princess_Theatre_at_night%2C_Launceston.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Princess_Theatre_at_night%2C_Launceston.JPG/330px-Princess_Theatre_at_night%2C_Launceston.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Princess_Theatre_at_night%2C_Launceston.JPG/440px-Princess_Theatre_at_night%2C_Launceston.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Princess_Theatre_at_night,_Launceston.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Theatre,_Launceston" title="Princess Theatre, Launceston">Princess Theatre</a> and Earl Arts Centre, <a href="/wiki/Launceston,_Tasmania" title="Launceston, Tasmania">Launceston</a></div></div></div><p>Tasmania has a varied musical scene, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Tasmanian Symphony Orchestra">Tasmanian Symphony Orchestra</a> whose home is the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Grand_Chancellor,_Hobart" title="Hotel Grand Chancellor, Hobart">Federation Concert Hall</a>, to a substantial number of small bands, orchestras, string quintets, saxophone ensembles and individual artists who perform at a variety of venues around the state. Tasmania is also home to a vibrant community of composers including <a href="/wiki/Constantine_Koukias" title="Constantine Koukias">Constantine Koukias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Grenfell" title="Maria Grenfell">Maria Grenfell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Don_Kay_(composer)" title="Don Kay (composer)">Don Kay</a>, who is the patron of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmanian_Composers_Collective&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tasmanian Composers Collective (page does not exist)">Tasmanian Composers Collective</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> the representative body for composers in Tasmania. Tasmania is also home to one of Australia's leading new music institutions, <a href="/wiki/IHOS_Music_Theatre_and_Opera" title="IHOS Music Theatre and Opera">IHOS Music Theatre and Opera</a> and gospel choirs, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Gospel_Choir" title="Southern Gospel Choir">Southern Gospel Choir</a>. Prominent Australian metal bands <a href="/wiki/Psycroptic" title="Psycroptic">Psycroptic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Striborg" title="Striborg">Striborg</a> hail from Tasmania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Noir-rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Paradise_Motel" title="The Paradise Motel">The Paradise Motel</a> and 1980s power-pop band <a href="/wiki/The_Innocents_(Australian_band)" title="The Innocents (Australian band)">The Innocents</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> are also citizens. <a href="/wiki/The_Mole_(Australia_season_1)" title="The Mole (Australia season 1)">The first season of</a> the television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mole_(Australian_TV_series)" title="The Mole (Australian TV series)">The Mole</a></i> was filmed and based mainly in Tasmania, with the final elimination taking place in <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur,_Tasmania" title="Port Arthur, Tasmania">Port Arthur</a> gaol.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tasmanian_cinema">Tasmanian cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Tasmanian cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Films set in Tasmania include <i><a href="/wiki/Young_Einstein" title="Young Einstein">Young Einstein</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tale_of_Ruby_Rose" title="The Tale of Ruby Rose">The Tale of Ruby Rose</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hunter_(2011_Australian_film)" title="The Hunter (2011 Australian film)">The Hunter</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Confession_of_Alexander_Pearce" title="The Last Confession of Alexander Pearce">The Last Confession of Alexander Pearce</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Arctic_Blast" title="Arctic Blast">Arctic Blast</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Manganinnie" title="Manganinnie">Manganinnie</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Van_Diemen%27s_Land_(film)" title="Van Diemen's Land (film)">Van Diemen's Land</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Lion_(2016_film)" title="Lion (2016 film)">Lion</a></i>. Common within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_cinema" title="Australian cinema">Australian cinema</a>, the Tasmanian landscape is a focal point in most of their feature film productions. <i>The Last Confession of Alexander Pearce</i> and <i>Van Diemen's Land</i> are both set during an episode of Tasmania's convict history. Tasmanian film production goes as far back as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silent_era" title="Silent era">silent era</a>, with the epic <i><a href="/wiki/For_the_Term_of_His_Natural_Life_(1927_film)" title="For the Term of His Natural Life (1927 film)">For The Term of his Natural Life</a></i> in 1927 being the most expensive feature film made on Australian shores. <a href="/wiki/The_Kettering_Incident" title="The Kettering Incident">The Kettering Incident</a> filmed in and around <a href="/wiki/Kettering,_Tasmania" title="Kettering, Tasmania">Kettering, Tasmania</a> won the 2016 AACTA Award for Best Telefeature or Mini Series.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Visual arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The biennial <i>Tasmanian Living Artists' Week</i> is a ten-day statewide festival for Tasmania's visual artists. The fourth festival in 2007 involved more than 1000 artists. Tasmania is home to two winners of the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Prize" title="Archibald Prize">Archibald Prize</a>—<a href="/wiki/Jack_Carington_Smith" title="Jack Carington Smith">Jack Carington Smith</a> in 1963 for a portrait of Professor <a href="/wiki/James_McAuley" title="James McAuley">James McAuley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Dyer" title="Geoffrey Dyer">Geoffrey Dyer</a> in 2003 for his portrait of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Flanagan" title="Richard Flanagan">Richard Flanagan</a>. Photographers <a href="/wiki/Olegas_Truchanas" title="Olegas Truchanas">Olegas Truchanas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dombrovskis" title="Peter Dombrovskis">Peter Dombrovskis</a> are known for works that became iconic in the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pedder" title="Lake Pedder">Lake Pedder</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franklin_Dam" title="Franklin Dam">Franklin Dam</a> conservation movements. English-born painter <a href="/wiki/John_Glover_(artist)" title="John Glover (artist)">John Glover</a> (1767–1849) is known for his paintings of Tasmanian landscapes. The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Old_and_New_Art" title="Museum of Old and New Art">Museum of Old and New Art</a> (MONA) opened in January 2011 at the <a href="/wiki/Moorilla_Estate" title="Moorilla Estate">Moorilla Estate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Berriedale,_Tasmania" title="Berriedale, Tasmania">Berriedale</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and is the largest privately owned museum complex in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HobartAirportTerminal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/HobartAirportTerminal.jpg/220px-HobartAirportTerminal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/HobartAirportTerminal.jpg/330px-HobartAirportTerminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/HobartAirportTerminal.jpg/440px-HobartAirportTerminal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HobartAirportTerminal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hobart_International_Airport" title="Hobart International Airport">Hobart International Airport</a>.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tasmania's main air carriers are <a href="/wiki/Jetstar_Airways" title="Jetstar Airways">Jetstar Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Australia" title="Virgin Australia">Virgin Australia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">Qantas</a>, <a href="/wiki/QantasLink" title="QantasLink">QantasLink</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regional_Express_Airlines" title="Regional Express Airlines">Regional Express Airlines</a>. These airlines fly direct routes to <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">the Gold Coast</a>, Melbourne and Sydney. Major airports include <a href="/wiki/Hobart_International_Airport" title="Hobart International Airport">Hobart International Airport</a> (which has not had a regular scheduled international passenger service since the 1990s) and <a href="/wiki/Launceston_Airport" title="Launceston Airport">Launceston Airport</a>; the smaller airports, <a href="/wiki/Burnie_Airport" title="Burnie Airport">Burnie</a> (Wynyard) and <a href="/wiki/King_Island_Airport" title="King Island Airport">King Island</a>, serviced by Regional Express; and <a href="/wiki/Devonport_Airport" title="Devonport Airport">Devonport</a>, serviced by QantasLink; have services to <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Airport" title="Melbourne Airport">Melbourne</a>. Intra-Tasmanian air services are offered by <a href="/wiki/Airlines_of_Tasmania" title="Airlines of Tasmania">Airlines of Tasmania</a>. Until 2001 <a href="/wiki/Ansett_Australia" title="Ansett Australia">Ansett Australia</a> operated majorly out of Tasmania to 12 destinations nationwide.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antarctica_base">Antarctica base</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Antarctica base">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tasmania – Hobart in particular – serves as Australia's chief sea link to Antarctica, with the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Antarctic_Division" title="Australian Antarctic Division">Australian Antarctic Division</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Tasmania" title="Kingston, Tasmania">Kingston</a>. Hobart is also the home port of the French ship <i>l'Astrolabe</i>, which makes regular supply runs to the <a href="/wiki/French_Southern_and_Antarctic_Lands" title="French Southern and Antarctic Lands">French Southern Territories</a> near and in Antarctica.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bridgewater_Bridge,_Tasmania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1680" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bridgewater_Bridge%2C_Tasmania.jpg/220px-Bridgewater_Bridge%2C_Tasmania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bridgewater_Bridge%2C_Tasmania.jpg/330px-Bridgewater_Bridge%2C_Tasmania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bridgewater_Bridge%2C_Tasmania.jpg/440px-Bridgewater_Bridge%2C_Tasmania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bridgewater_Bridge,_Tasmania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bridgewater Bridge</div></div></div>
<p>Within the state, the primary form of transport is by road. Since the 1980s, many of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highways_in_Tasmania" title="List of highways in Tasmania">state's highways</a> have undergone regular upgrades. These include the Hobart <a href="/wiki/Southern_Outlet,_Hobart" title="Southern Outlet, Hobart">Southern Outlet</a>, Launceston Southern Outlet, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bass_Highway_(Tasmania)" title="Bass Highway (Tasmania)">Bass Highway</a> reconstruction, and the <a href="/wiki/Huon_Highway" title="Huon Highway">Huon Highway</a>. Public transport is provided by <a href="/wiki/Metro_Tasmania" title="Metro Tasmania">Metro Tasmania</a> bus services, regular taxis and Hobart only<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> UBER ride-share services within urban areas, with <a href="/wiki/Redline_Coaches" title="Redline Coaches">Redline Coaches</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tassielink_Transit" title="Tassielink Transit">Tassielink Transit</a> and Callows Coaches providing bus service between population centres.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Tasmania" title="Rail transport in Tasmania">Rail transport in Tasmania</a> consists of narrow-gauge lines to all four major population centres and to mining and forestry operations on the west coast and in the northwest. Services are operated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TasRail_(2009)" title="TasRail (2009)">TasRail</a>. Regular passenger train services in the state ceased in 1977; the only scheduled trains are for freight, but there are tourist trains in specific areas, for example the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Wilderness_Railway" title="West Coast Wilderness Railway">West Coast Wilderness Railway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ida_Bay_Railway" title="Ida Bay Railway">Ida Bay Railway</a>. There is an <a href="/wiki/Riverline_(Hobart)" title="Riverline (Hobart)">ongoing proposal</a> to reinstate commuter trains to Hobart. This idea however lacks political motivation.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipping">Shipping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Shipping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bass_Strait_Ferries" title="Bass Strait Ferries">Bass Strait Ferries</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spirit_of_Tasmania_Port_Melbourne.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1432" data-file-width="2563" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Spirit_of_Tasmania_Port_Melbourne.jpg/220px-Spirit_of_Tasmania_Port_Melbourne.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Spirit_of_Tasmania_Port_Melbourne.jpg/330px-Spirit_of_Tasmania_Port_Melbourne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Spirit_of_Tasmania_Port_Melbourne.jpg/440px-Spirit_of_Tasmania_Port_Melbourne.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spirit_of_Tasmania_Port_Melbourne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i><a href="/wiki/MS_Spirit_of_Tasmania_II" title="MS Spirit of Tasmania II">Spirit of Tasmania</a></i> links the island with mainland Australia.</div></div></div>
<p>The port of Hobart is the second deepest natural port in the world, second to only <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> in Brazil.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There is a substantial amount of commercial and recreational shipping within the harbour, and the port hosts approximately 120 cruise ships during the warmer half of the year, and there are occasional visits from military vessels.
</p><p><a class="external free" href="http://www.premier.tas.gov.au/releases/tasports_continues_to_deliver_strong_results" rel="nofollow">http://www.premier.tas.gov.au/releases/tasports_continues_to_deliver_strong_results</a>
</p><p>Burnie and Devonport on the northwest coast host ports and several other coastal towns host either small fishing ports or substantial marinas. The domestic sea route between Tasmanian and the mainland is serviced by <a href="/wiki/Bass_Strait" title="Bass Strait">Bass Strait</a> passenger/vehicle ferries operated by the Tasmanian government-owned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TT-Line_(Australia)" title="TT-Line (Australia)">TT-Line (Tasmania)</a>. The state is also home to <a href="/wiki/Incat" title="Incat">Incat</a>, a manufacturer of very high-speed aluminium catamarans that regularly broke records when they were first launched. The state government tried using them on the Bass Strait run but eventually decided to discontinue the run because of concerns over viability and the suitability of the vessels for the extreme weather conditions sometimes experienced in the strait.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Tasmania" title="Sport in Tasmania">Sport in Tasmania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:One-day_Cricket_Australia_vs_England,_Bellerive_Oval,_January_2011_(2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2672" data-file-width="4008" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/One-day_Cricket_Australia_vs_England%2C_Bellerive_Oval%2C_January_2011_%282%29.jpg/220px-One-day_Cricket_Australia_vs_England%2C_Bellerive_Oval%2C_January_2011_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/One-day_Cricket_Australia_vs_England%2C_Bellerive_Oval%2C_January_2011_%282%29.jpg/330px-One-day_Cricket_Australia_vs_England%2C_Bellerive_Oval%2C_January_2011_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/One-day_Cricket_Australia_vs_England%2C_Bellerive_Oval%2C_January_2011_%282%29.jpg/440px-One-day_Cricket_Australia_vs_England%2C_Bellerive_Oval%2C_January_2011_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:One-day_Cricket_Australia_vs_England,_Bellerive_Oval,_January_2011_(2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bellerive_Oval" title="Bellerive Oval">Bellerive Oval</a> at night, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One-day_cricket" title="One-day cricket">one-day cricket</a> Australia vs England.</div></div></div>
<p>Sport is an important pastime in Tasmania, and the state has produced several famous sportsmen and women and also hosted several major sporting events. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Tigers" title="Tasmanian Tigers">Tasmanian Tigers</a> cricket team represents the state successfully (for example the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Shield" title="Sheffield Shield">Sheffield Shield</a> in 2007, 2011 and 2013) and plays its home games at the <a href="/wiki/Bellerive_Oval" title="Bellerive Oval">Bellerive Oval</a> in Hobart; which is also the home ground for the Hobart Hurricanes in the Big Bash League. In addition, Bellerive Oval regularly hosts international cricket matches. Famous Tasmanian cricketers include <a href="/wiki/David_Boon" title="David Boon">David Boon</a> and former Australian captain <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Ponting" title="Ricky Ponting">Ricky Ponting</a>.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Rules_Football" title="Australian Rules Football">Australian Rules Football</a> is also popularly followed, with frequent discussion of a proposed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_AFL_Bid" title="Tasmanian AFL Bid">Tasmanian team</a> in the Australian Football League (<a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">AFL</a>). Several AFL games have been played at <a href="/wiki/York_Park" title="York Park">Aurora Stadium</a>, Launceston, including the <a href="/wiki/Hawthorn_Football_Club" title="Hawthorn Football Club">Hawthorn Football Club</a> and as of  2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, at the Bellerive Oval with the <a href="/wiki/North_Melbourne_Football_Club" title="North Melbourne Football Club">North Melbourne Football Club</a> playing 3 home games there. The stadium was the site of an infamous match between <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda_Football_Club" title="St Kilda Football Club">St Kilda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fremantle_Football_Club" title="Fremantle Football Club">Fremantle</a> which was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AFL_siren_controversy,_2006" title="AFL siren controversy, 2006">controversially drawn</a> after the umpires failed to hear the final siren.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby league</a> football is also played in the area, with the highest level of football played is in the <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Rugby_League" title="Tasmanian Rugby League">Tasmanian Rugby League</a> competition. The most successful team is the Hobart Tigers winning the title three times.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rugby_Union" title="Rugby Union">Rugby Union</a> is also played in Tasmania and is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Rugby_Union" title="Tasmanian Rugby Union">Tasmanian Rugby Union</a>. Ten clubs take part in the statewide Tasmanian Rugby Competition.
</p><p>Association football (soccer) is played throughout the state, including a proposed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmania_United_FC" title="Tasmania United FC">Tasmanian A-League Club</a> and an existing statewide league called the <a href="/wiki/National_Premier_Leagues_Tasmania" title="National Premier Leagues Tasmania">NPL Tasmania</a>.
</p><p>Tasmania hosts the professional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moorilla_Hobart_International" title="Moorilla Hobart International">Moorilla International</a> tennis tournament as part of the lead up to the Australian Open and is played at the <a href="/wiki/Hobart_International_Tennis_Centre" title="Hobart International Tennis Centre">Hobart International Tennis Centre</a>, Hobart.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sydney_to_Hobart_Yacht_Race" title="Sydney to Hobart Yacht Race">Sydney to Hobart Yacht Race</a> is an annual event starting in Sydney, NSW, on Boxing Day and finishing in Hobart, Tasmania. It is widely considered to be one of the most difficult yacht races in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>While some of the other sports played and barracked for have grown in popularity, others have declined. For example, in basketball Tasmania has not been represented in the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_League_(Australia)" title="National Basketball League (Australia)">National Basketball League</a> since the demise of the <a href="/wiki/Hobart_Devils" title="Hobart Devils">Hobart Devils</a> in 1996.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Tasmanians" title="List of Tasmanians">List of Tasmanians</a></div>
<p>Notable people from Tasmania include:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Truganini" title="Truganini">Truganini</a>, full-blooded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Aborigine" title="Tasmanian Aborigine">Tasmanian Aborigine</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/John_Gellibrand" title="John Gellibrand">John Gellibrand</a>, founder of Legacy</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Graeme_Murphy" title="Graeme Murphy">Graeme Murphy</a>, dancer and choreographer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Errol_Flynn" title="Errol Flynn">Errol Flynn</a>, actor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nan_Chauncy" title="Nan Chauncy">Nan Chauncy</a>, author</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politicians">Politicians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Politicians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lyons" title="Joseph Lyons">Joseph Lyons</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">Prime Minister of Australia</a></li>
<li>his wife Dame <a href="/wiki/Enid_Lyons" title="Enid Lyons">Enid Lyons</a>, the first woman member of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_House_of_Representatives" title="Australian House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Brown" title="Bob Brown">Bob Brown</a>, former leader of the Greens political party</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Actors">Actors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Actors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Actor <a href="/wiki/Simon_Baker" title="Simon Baker">Simon Baker</a>, star of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mentalist" title="The Mentalist">The Mentalist</a></i></li>
<li>Actor <a href="/wiki/Errol_Flynn" title="Errol Flynn">Errol Flynn</a></li>
<li>Actress <a href="/wiki/Rachael_Taylor" title="Rachael Taylor">Rachael Taylor</a></li>
<li>Australian actress <a href="/wiki/Kris_McQuade" title="Kris McQuade">Kris McQuade</a> lives in Tasmania.</li>
<li>Actress <a href="/wiki/Essie_Davis" title="Essie Davis">Essie Davis</a>, star of <i><a href="/wiki/Miss_Fisher%27s_Murder_Mysteries" title="Miss Fisher's Murder Mysteries">Miss Fisher's Murder Mysteries</a></i></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Authors">Authors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Authors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Flanagan" title="Richard Flanagan">Richard Flanagan</a>, Australian author and recipient of the Man Booker Prize 2014</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Katherine_Scholes" title="Katherine Scholes">Katherine Scholes</a>, Australian author</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rachael_Treasure" title="Rachael Treasure">Rachael Treasure</a>, Australian author</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Brown" title="Bob Brown">Bob Brown</a>, Australian author</li>

<li>Cartoonist <a href="/wiki/Simon_Hanselmann" title="Simon Hanselmann">Simon Hanselmann</a>, best best known for his <i>Megg, Mogg, and Owl</i> series of comics</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_persons">Sports persons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Sports persons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

Although, he was born in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>.</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musicians_and_composers">Musicians and composers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tasmania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Musicians and composers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Musician <a href="/wiki/Courtney_Barnett" title="Courtney Barnett">Courtney Barnett</a> (born in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>; however, she moved to <a href="/wiki/Hobart" title="Hobart">Hobart</a> with her family at age sixteen, attending <a href="/wiki/St_Michael%27s_Collegiate_School" title="St Michael's Collegiate School">St Michael's Collegiate School</a> and later, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tasmania" title="University of Tasmania">Tasmanian School of Art</a>)</li>
<li>Drummer <a href="/wiki/Dave_Haley" title="Dave Haley">Dave Haley</a> from technical death metal band <a href="/wiki/Psycroptic" title="Psycroptic">Psycroptic</a> and black metal band <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruins_(metal_band)" title="Ruins (metal band)">Ruins (metal band)</a></li>

<li>Composer <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sculthorpe" title="Peter Sculthorpe">Peter Sculthorpe</a></li>
<li>Band <a href="/wiki/Luca_Brasi_(band)" title="Luca Brasi (band)">Luca Brasi (band)</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="per WP:CIRCULAR (June 2018)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Bassist <a href="/wiki/Brian_Ritchie" title="Brian Ritchie">Brian Ritchie</a>, founding member of <a href="/wiki/Violent_Femmes" title="Violent Femmes">Violent Femmes</a></li>
<li>Musician Russell Menzies (Sin Nanna) of one-man black metal band <a href="/wiki/Striborg" title="Striborg">Striborg</a></li>
